</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Latin_America" title="History of Latin America">History of Latin America</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_North_America" title="History of North America">History of North America</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_America" title="History of South America">History of South America</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Central_America" title="History of Central America">History of Central America</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Caribbean" title="History of the Caribbean">History of the Caribbean</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_history">Pre-Columbian history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Settlement_of_the_Americas" title="Settlement of the Americas">Settlement of the Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Population_history_of_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Population history of indigenous peoples of the Americas">Population history of indigenous peoples of the Americas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">Pre-Columbian era</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:175px;"><a href="/wiki/File:80_-_Machu_Picchu_-_Juin_2009_-_edit.2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/80_-_Machu_Picchu_-_Juin_2009_-_edit.2.jpg/173px-80_-_Machu_Picchu_-_Juin_2009_-_edit.2.jpg" decoding="async" width="173" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/80_-_Machu_Picchu_-_Juin_2009_-_edit.2.jpg/260px-80_-_Machu_Picchu_-_Juin_2009_-_edit.2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/80_-_Machu_Picchu_-_Juin_2009_-_edit.2.jpg/346px-80_-_Machu_Picchu_-_Juin_2009_-_edit.2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10000" data-file-height="9760" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:80_-_Machu_Picchu_-_Juin_2009_-_edit.2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of <a href="/wiki/Machu_Picchu" title="Machu Picchu">Machu Picchu</a>, a pre-Columbian <a href="/wiki/Inca" class="mw-redirect" title="Inca">Inca</a> site in <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chichen_Itza_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Chichen_Itza_3.jpg/220px-Chichen_Itza_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Chichen_Itza_3.jpg/330px-Chichen_Itza_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Chichen_Itza_3.jpg/440px-Chichen_Itza_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="9771" data-file-height="5197" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chichen_Itza_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Maya_Civilization" class="mw-redirect" title="Maya Civilization">Mayan</a> archeological site <a href="/wiki/Chichen_Itza" title="Chichen Itza">Chichen Itza</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The earliest known settlement was identified at <a href="/wiki/Monte_Verde" title="Monte Verde">Monte Verde</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Montt" title="Puerto Montt">Puerto Montt</a> in Southern Chile. Its occupation dates to some 14,000 years ago and there is some disputed evidence of even earlier occupation. Over the course of millennia, people spread to all parts of the continents. By the first millennium <a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">CE</a>, South America's vast rainforests, mountains, plains and coasts were the home of tens of millions of people. The earliest settlements in the Americas are of the <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_culture_(archaeology)" title="Las Vegas culture (archaeology)">Las Vegas Culture</a><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> from about 8000&#160;BCE and 4600&#160;BCE, a sedentary group from the coast of <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, the forefathers of the more known <a href="/wiki/Valdivia_culture" title="Valdivia culture">Valdivia culture</a>, of the same era. Some groups formed more permanent settlements such as the <a href="/wiki/Chibcha_language" title="Chibcha language">Chibcha</a> (or "<a href="/wiki/Muisca_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Muisca people">Muisca</a>" or "Muysca") and the <a href="/wiki/Tairona" title="Tairona">Tairona</a> groups. These groups are in the circum Caribbean region. The Chibchas of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Quechuas" class="mw-redirect" title="Quechuas">Quechuas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aymaras" class="mw-redirect" title="Aymaras">Aymaras</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> were the three indigenous groups that settled most permanently.
</p><p>The region was home to many <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a> and advanced civilizations, including the <a href="/wiki/Aztecs" title="Aztecs">Aztecs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toltecs" class="mw-redirect" title="Toltecs">Toltecs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maya_Civilization" class="mw-redirect" title="Maya Civilization">Maya</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Inca" class="mw-redirect" title="Inca">Inca</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Golden_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden age">golden age</a> of the Maya began about 250, with the last two great <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilizations</a>, the Aztecs and Incas, emerging into prominence later on in the early fourteenth century and mid-fifteenth centuries, respectively. The Aztec empire was ultimately the most powerful civilization known throughout the Americas, until its downfall in part by the Spanish invasion.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_colonization">European colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: European colonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonization of the Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish colonization of the Americas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Portuguese colonization of the Americas">Portuguese colonization of the Americas</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Desembarco_de_Col%C3%B3n_de_Di%C3%B3scoro_Puebla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Desembarco_de_Col%C3%B3n_de_Di%C3%B3scoro_Puebla.jpg/250px-Desembarco_de_Col%C3%B3n_de_Di%C3%B3scoro_Puebla.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Desembarco_de_Col%C3%B3n_de_Di%C3%B3scoro_Puebla.jpg/375px-Desembarco_de_Col%C3%B3n_de_Di%C3%B3scoro_Puebla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Desembarco_de_Col%C3%B3n_de_Di%C3%B3scoro_Puebla.jpg/500px-Desembarco_de_Col%C3%B3n_de_Di%C3%B3scoro_Puebla.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1161" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Desembarco_de_Col%C3%B3n_de_Di%C3%B3scoro_Puebla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">Romantic</a> painting of Italian explorer <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> arriving to the Americas (<i>Primer desembarco de Cristóbal Colón en América</i>), by <a href="/wiki/Di%C3%B3scoro_Puebla" title="Dióscoro Puebla">Dióscoro Puebla</a> (1862)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jal-ixco.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Jal-ixco.jpg/250px-Jal-ixco.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Jal-ixco.jpg/375px-Jal-ixco.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Jal-ixco.jpg/500px-Jal-ixco.jpg 2x" data-file-width="606" data-file-height="493" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jal-ixco.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Crist%C3%B3bal_de_Olid" title="Cristóbal de Olid">Cristóbal de Olid</a> leads <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish</a> soldiers with <a href="/wiki/Tlaxcala_(Nahua_state)" title="Tlaxcala (Nahua state)">Tlaxcalan</a> allies against <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous warriors</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">European colonization of the Americas</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>With the arrival of the Europeans following <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>' voyages, the indigenous elites, such as the Incas and Aztecs, lost power to the heavy European invasion. <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1ndo_Cort%C3%A9s" class="mw-redirect" title="Hernándo Cortés">Hernándo Cortés</a> seized the Aztec elite's power with the help of local groups who had favored the Aztec elite, and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Pizarro" title="Francisco Pizarro">Francisco Pizarro</a> eliminated the Incan rule in Western South America. The European powers of Spain and Portugal colonized the region, which along with the rest of the uncolonized world, was divided into areas of Spanish and Portuguese control by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">line of demarcation</a> in 1494, which gave Spain all areas to the west, and Portugal all areas to the east (the Portuguese lands in South America subsequently becoming Brazil). By the end of the sixteenth century Spain and Portugal had been joined by others, including France, in occupying large areas of North, Central and South America, ultimately extending from Alaska to the southern tips of the <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a>. European culture, customs and government were introduced, with the Roman Catholic Church becoming the major economic and political power to overrule the traditional ways of the region, eventually becoming the only official religion of the Americas during this period.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg/220px-Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg/330px-Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg/440px-Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2655" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spanish and Portuguese empires in 1790.</div></div></div>
<p>Epidemics of diseases brought by the Europeans, such as <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>, wiped out a large portion of the indigenous population. Historians cannot determine the number of natives who died due to European diseases, but some put the figures as high as 85% and as low as 25%. Due to the lack of written records, specific numbers are hard to verify. Many of the survivors were forced to work in European plantations and mines. <a href="/wiki/Miscegenation" title="Miscegenation">Intermixing</a> between the indigenous peoples and the European colonists was very common, and, by the end of the <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonial period</a>, people of mixed ancestry (<a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizos</a>) formed majorities in several colonies.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Slavery_and_forced_labor_in_colonial_Latin_America">Slavery and forced labor in colonial Latin America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Slavery and forced labor in colonial Latin America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Slavery_among_the_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Slavery among the indigenous peoples of the Americas">Slavery among the indigenous peoples of the Americas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a></div>
<p>Indigenous peoples of the Americas in various European colonies were forced to work in European plantations and mines; along with African slaves who were also introduced in the proceeding centuries.
</p><p>The Mita of Colonial Latin America was a system of forced labor imposed on the natives. First established by Viceroy Francisco de Toledo (1569–1581), the Mita was upheld by laws that designated how large draft levies were and how much money the workers would receive that was based on how many shifts each individual worker performed. Toledo established Mitas at Potosi and Huancavelica, where the Mitayos—the workers—would be reduced in number to a fraction of how many were originally assigned before the 1700s. While several villages managed to resist the Mita, others offered payment to colonial administrators as a way out. In exchange, free labor became available through volunteers, though the Mita was kept in place as workers like miners, for example, were paid low wages. The Spanish Crown had not made any ruling on the Mita or approved of it when Toledo first established it in spite of the uncertainty of the practice since the Crown could have gained benefits from it. However, the cortes of Spain later abolished it in 1812 once complaints of the Mita violating humanitarian rights were made. Yet complaints also came from: governors; landowners; native leaders known as Kurakas; and even priests, each of whom preferred other methods of economic exploitation. Despite its fall, the Mita made it to the 1800s.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another important group of slaves to mention were the slaves brought over from Africa. The first slaves came over with Christopher Columbus from the very beginning on his earliest voyages. However in the few hundred years, the Atlantic Slave trade would begin delivering slaves, imported by Spain and other colonizers, by the millions. Many of the large scale productions were run by forced slave labor. They were a part of sugar and coffee production, farming (beans, rice, corn, fruit, etc.), Mining, whale oil and multiple other jobs. Slaves were also house workers, servants, military soldiers, and much more. To say the least these people were property and treated as such. Though indigenous slaves existed, they were no match in quantity and lack of quality jobs when compared to the African slave. The slave population was massive compared to the better known slave ownership in the United States. After 1860 Brazil alone had imported over 4 million slaves, which only represented about 35% of the Atlantic slave trade. Despite the large number of slaves in Latin America, there was not as much reproduction of slaves amongst the population. Because most of the slaves then were African-born, they were more subject to rebellion. The United States involvement in the slave trade is well known amongst North America, however it hides a larger and in some ways crueler operation in the south which had a much longer history.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Independence_.281804.E2.80.931825.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1804–1825)">Independence (1804–1825)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Independence (1804–1825)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_wars_of_independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin American wars of independence">Latin American wars of independence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolivar_Arturo_Michelena.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bolivar_Arturo_Michelena.jpg/140px-Bolivar_Arturo_Michelena.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="280" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bolivar_Arturo_Michelena.jpg/210px-Bolivar_Arturo_Michelena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bolivar_Arturo_Michelena.jpg/280px-Bolivar_Arturo_Michelena.jpg 2x" data-file-width="874" data-file-height="1748" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolivar_Arturo_Michelena.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a>, Liberator of <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1804, Haiti became the first Latin American nation to gain independence, following a violent slave revolt led by <a href="/wiki/Toussaint_L%27ouverture" class="mw-redirect" title="Toussaint L&#39;ouverture">Toussaint L'ouverture</a> on the French colony of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a>. The victors abolished slavery. Haitian independence inspired independence movements in Spanish America.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Hidalgo_y_Costilla.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Miguel_Hidalgo_y_Costilla.png/140px-Miguel_Hidalgo_y_Costilla.png" decoding="async" width="140" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Miguel_Hidalgo_y_Costilla.png/210px-Miguel_Hidalgo_y_Costilla.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Miguel_Hidalgo_y_Costilla.png/280px-Miguel_Hidalgo_y_Costilla.png 2x" data-file-width="459" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Hidalgo_y_Costilla.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Miguel_Hidalgo_y_Costilla" title="Miguel Hidalgo y Costilla">Miguel Hidalgo y Costilla</a> was the first leader of the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">Mexican War of Independence</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>By the end of the eighteenth century, Spanish and Portuguese power waned on the global scene as other European powers took their place, notably Britain and France. Resentment grew among the majority of the population in Latin America over the restrictions imposed by the Spanish government, as well as the dominance of native Spaniards (Iberian-born <i><a href="/wiki/Peninsulares" class="mw-redirect" title="Peninsulares">Peninsulares</a></i>) in the major social and political <a href="/wiki/Institution" title="Institution">institutions</a>. <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>'s invasion of Spain in 1808 marked a turning point, compelling <a href="/wiki/Criollo_people" title="Criollo people">Criollo</a> elites to form <a href="/wiki/Junta_(Peninsular_War)" title="Junta (Peninsular War)">juntas</a> that advocated independence. Also, the newly independent <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, the second oldest nation in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> after the United States, further fueled the independence movement by inspiring the leaders of the movement, such as <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Hidalgo_y_Costilla" title="Miguel Hidalgo y Costilla">Miguel Hidalgo y Costilla</a> of Mexico, <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a> of Venezuela and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="José de San Martín">José de San Martín</a> of Argentina, and by providing them with considerable munitions and troops.
</p><p>Fighting soon broke out between juntas and the Spanish colonial authorities, with initial victories for the advocates of independence. Eventually, these early movements were crushed by the <a href="/wiki/Royalist_(Hispanic_American_Revolution)" class="mw-redirect" title="Royalist (Hispanic American Revolution)">royalist troops</a> by 1810, including those of <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Hidalgo_y_Costilla" title="Miguel Hidalgo y Costilla">Miguel Hidalgo y Costilla</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> in the year 1810. Later on <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Miranda" title="Francisco de Miranda">Francisco de Miranda</a> in <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> by 1812. Under the leadership of a new generation of leaders, such as <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a> "The Liberator", <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="José de San Martín">José de San Martín</a> of Argentina, and other <i><a href="/wiki/Libertadores" title="Libertadores">Libertadores</a></i> in South America, the independence movement regained strength, and by 1825, all <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">Spanish America</a>, except for Puerto Rico and Cuba, had gained independence from Spain. In the same year in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, a military officer, <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_de_Iturbide" title="Agustín de Iturbide">Agustín de Iturbide</a>, led a coalition of conservatives and liberals who created a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>, with Iturbide as <a href="/wiki/Emperor" title="Emperor">emperor</a>. This <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">First Mexican Empire</a> was short-lived, and was followed by the creation of a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> in 1823.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_Empire_of_Brazil">Independent Empire of Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Independent Empire of Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">Independence of Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_(1888).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_%281888%29.jpg/260px-Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_%281888%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_%281888%29.jpg/390px-Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_%281888%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_%281888%29.jpg/520px-Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_%281888%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2271" data-file-height="1268" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Independ%C3%AAncia_ou_Morte_(1888).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Declaration of the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Independence_of_Brazil" title="War of Independence of Brazil">Brazilian independence</a> by the later <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Emperor Pedro&#160;I</a> on September 7, 1822</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_War_of_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian War of Independence">Brazilian War of Independence</a>, which had already begun along other independent movements around the region, spread through northern, northeastern regions and in Cisplatina province.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-44">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> With the last Portuguese soldiers surrendering on 8 March 1824,<sup id="cite_ref-Diégues_2004,_pp._179–180_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diégues_2004,_pp._179–180-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Portugal officially recognized Brazil on 29 August 1825.<sup id="cite_ref-Lustosa,_p._208_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lustosa,_p._208-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 April 1831, worn down by years of administrative turmoil and political dissensions with both liberal and conservative sides of politics, including an attempt of <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Equator" title="Confederation of the Equator">republican secession</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ibidem_Fausto_1999,_pages_82–83_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ibidem_Fausto_1999,_pages_82–83-47">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> as well as unreconciled with the way that absolutists in Portugal had given to the succession of King John VI, Pedro&#160;I went to Portugal to <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Wars" title="Liberal Wars">reclaim his daughter's crown</a>, abdicating the Brazilian throne in favor of his five-year-old son and heir (who thus became the Empire's second monarch, with the regnal title of Dom <a href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Brazil" title="Pedro II of Brazil">Pedro&#160;II</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Lyra_v.1,_p._17_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyra_v.1,_p._17-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg/170px-Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg/255px-Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg/340px-Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="876" data-file-height="1281" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Brazil" title="Pedro II of Brazil">Pedro II</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_Brazil" title="List of monarchs of Brazil">Emperor of Brazil</a> between 1831 and 1889</div></div></div>
<p>As the new Emperor could not exert his constitutional powers until he became of age, a <a href="/wiki/Regency_(government)" class="mw-redirect" title="Regency (government)">regency</a> was set up by the National Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> In the absence of a charismatic figure who could represent a moderate face of power, during this period a series of localized rebellions took place, as the <a href="/wiki/Cabanagem" title="Cabanagem">Cabanagem</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%AA_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Malê Revolt">Malê Revolt</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Balaiada" title="Balaiada">Balaiada</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sabinada" title="Sabinada">Sabinada</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ragamuffin_War" title="Ragamuffin War">Ragamuffin War</a>, which emerged from the dissatisfaction of the provinces with the central power, coupled with old and latent social tensions peculiar of a vast, slaveholding and newly independent <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">nation state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> This period of internal political and social upheaval, which included the <a href="/wiki/Praieira_revolt" title="Praieira revolt">Praieira revolt</a>, was overcome only at the end of the 1840s, years after the end of the regency, which occurred with the <a href="/wiki/Dom_Pedro_II#Early_coronation" class="mw-redirect" title="Dom Pedro II">premature coronation of Pedro II</a> in 1841.<sup id="cite_ref-Ibidem_Fausto_1999_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ibidem_Fausto_1999-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the last phase of the monarchy, an internal political debate was centered on the issue of slavery. The <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a> was abandoned in 1850,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> as a result of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">British</a>' <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_Act" title="Aberdeen Act">Aberdeen Act</a>, but only in <a href="/wiki/Lei_%C3%81urea" title="Lei Áurea">May 1888</a> after a long process of internal mobilization and debate for an ethical and legal dismantling of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Brazil" title="Slavery in Brazil">slavery in the country</a>, was the institution formally abolished.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 November 1889, worn out by years of economic stagnation, in attrition with the majority of Army officers, as well as with rural and financial elites (for different reasons), the monarchy was overthrown by a military coup.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Conservative.E2.80.93liberal_conflicts_in_the_19th_century"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservative–liberal_conflicts_in_the_19th_century">Conservative–liberal conflicts in the 19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Conservative–liberal conflicts in the 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hisparevol.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Hisparevol.gif/250px-Hisparevol.gif" decoding="async" width="250" height="323" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Hisparevol.gif/375px-Hisparevol.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/31/Hisparevol.gif 2x" data-file-width="470" data-file-height="608" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hisparevol.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><br /><b>Development of Spanish American Independence</b><br /><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Government under traditional Spanish law</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFA500; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Loyal to Supreme Central Junta or Cortes</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFFF00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;American junta or insurrection movement</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #008000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Independent state declared or established</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Height of French control of the Peninsula</div></div></div></div>
<p>After the independence of many Latin American countries, there was a conflict between the people and the government, much of which can be reduced to the contrasting ideologies between liberalism and conservatism.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Conservatism was the dominant system of government prior to the revolutions and it was founded on having social classes, including governing by kings. Liberalists wanted to see a change in the ruling systems, and to move away from monarchs and social classes in order to promote equality.
</p><p>When liberal <a href="/wiki/Guadalupe_Victoria" title="Guadalupe Victoria">Guadalupe Victoria</a> became the first president of Mexico in 1824, conservatists relied on their belief that the state had been better off before the new government came into power, so, by comparison, the old government was better in the eyes of the Conservatives. Following this sentiment, the conservatives pushed to take control of the government, and they succeeded. <a href="/wiki/General_Santa_Anna" class="mw-redirect" title="General Santa Anna">General Santa Anna</a> was elected president in 1833. The following decade, the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a> (1846–48) caused Mexico to lose a significant amount of territory to the United States. This loss led to a rebellion by the enraged liberal forces against the conservative government.
</p><p>In 1837, conservative <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Carrera" title="Rafael Carrera">Rafael Carrera</a> conquered <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a> and separated from the <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Central American Union">Central American Union</a>. The instability that followed the disintegration of the union led to the independence of the other Central American countries.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, rural aristocrats were in conflict with the urban conservatives. Portuguese control over Brazilian ports continued after Brazil's independence. Following the conservative idea that the old government was better, urbanites tended to support conservatism because more opportunities were available to them as a result of the Portuguese presence.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a> became president of <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Gran Colombia</a> in 1819 after the region gained independence from Spain. He led a military-controlled state. Citizens did not like the government's position under Bolívar: The people in the military were unhappy with their roles, and the civilians were of the opinion that the military had too much power. After the dissolution of Gran Colombia, New Grenada continued to have conflicts between conservatives and liberals. These conflicts were each concentrated in particular regions, with conservatives particularly in the southern mountains and the Valley of Cauca. In the mid-1840s some leaders in Caracas organized a liberal opposition. Antonio Leocadio Guzman was an active participant and journalist in this movement and gained much popularity among the people of Caracas.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, the conflict manifested itself as a prolonged civil war between <i><a href="/wiki/Unitarian_Party" title="Unitarian Party">unitarianas</a></i> (i.e. <i>centralists</i>) and <i><a href="/wiki/Federales" title="Federales">federalists</a></i>, which were in some aspects respectively analogous to liberals and conservatives in other countries. Between 1832 and 1852, the country existed as a <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Confederation" title="Argentine Confederation">confederation</a>, without a head of state, although the federalist governor of Buenos Aires province, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_de_Rosas" title="Juan Manuel de Rosas">Juan Manuel de Rosas</a>, was given the powers of debt payment and international relations and exerted a growing hegemony over the country. A national constitution was only enacted in 1853, reformed in 1860, and the country reorganized as a federal republic led by a <a href="/wiki/Generation_of_%2780" title="Generation of &#39;80">liberal-conservative elite</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> After Uruguay achieved its independence, in 1828, a similar polarization crystallized between <i>blancos</i> and <i>colorados</i>, where the agrarian conservative interests were pitted against the liberal commercial interests based in Montevideo, and which eventually resulted in the <i><a href="/wiki/Uruguayan_Civil_War" title="Uruguayan Civil War">Guerra Grande</a></i> civil war (1839–1851).<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_influence_in_Latin_America_during_the_19th_century">British influence in Latin America during the 19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: British influence in Latin America during the 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Reconquista_de_Buenos_Aires.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/74/La_Reconquista_de_Buenos_Aires.jpg/300px-La_Reconquista_de_Buenos_Aires.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/74/La_Reconquista_de_Buenos_Aires.jpg/450px-La_Reconquista_de_Buenos_Aires.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/74/La_Reconquista_de_Buenos_Aires.jpg/600px-La_Reconquista_de_Buenos_Aires.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="857" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Reconquista_de_Buenos_Aires.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/British_invasions_of_the_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" class="mw-redirect" title="British invasions of the Río de la Plata">British invasions of the Río de la Plata</a>. <a href="/wiki/William_Beresford,_1st_Viscount_Beresford" title="William Beresford, 1st Viscount Beresford">Beresford</a> surrenders to <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Liniers" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiago de Liniers">Santiago de Liniers</a> (1806).</div></div></div>
<p>Losing most of its North American colonies at the end of the 18th century left Great Britain in need of new markets to supply resources in the early 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Donghi,_T._1970_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Donghi,_T._1970-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In order to solve this problem, Great Britain turned to the Spanish colonies in South America for resources and markets. In 1806 a small British force surprise attacked the capitol of the viceroyalty in&#160;<a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="Río de la Plata">Río de la Plata</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>&#160;As a result, the local garrison protecting the capitol was destroyed in an attempt to defend against the British conquest. The British were able to capture large amounts of precious metals, before a French naval force intervened on behalf of the Spanish King and took down the invading force. However, this caused much turmoil in the area as militia took control of the area from the viceroy. The next year the British attacked once again with a much larger force attempting to reach and conquer Montevideo.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> They failed to reach <a href="/wiki/Montevideo" title="Montevideo">Montevideo</a> but succeeded in establishing an alliance with the locals. As a result, the British were able to take control of the Indian markets.
</p><p>This newly gained British dominance hindered the development of Latin American industries and strengthened the dependence on the world trade&#160;network.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Britain now replaced Spain as the region's largest trading&#160;partner.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>&#160;Great Britain invested significant capital in Latin America in order to develop the area as a market for processed goods.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> From the early 1820s to 1850, the post-independence economies of Latin American countries were lagging and stagnant.<sup id="cite_ref-Donghi,_T._1970_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Donghi,_T._1970-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Eventually, enhanced trade among Britain and Latin America led to state development such as infrastructure improvements. These improvements included roads and railroads which grew the trades between countries and outside nations such as Great Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> By 1870, exports dramatically increased, attracting capital from abroad (including Europe and USA).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_involvement_in_Latin_America_during_the_19th_century">French involvement in Latin America during the 19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: French involvement in Latin America during the 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dell%27Acqua_Ernennung_Maximilians_zum_Kaiser_Mexikos.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Dell%27Acqua_Ernennung_Maximilians_zum_Kaiser_Mexikos.jpg/280px-Dell%27Acqua_Ernennung_Maximilians_zum_Kaiser_Mexikos.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Dell%27Acqua_Ernennung_Maximilians_zum_Kaiser_Mexikos.jpg/420px-Dell%27Acqua_Ernennung_Maximilians_zum_Kaiser_Mexikos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Dell%27Acqua_Ernennung_Maximilians_zum_Kaiser_Mexikos.jpg/560px-Dell%27Acqua_Ernennung_Maximilians_zum_Kaiser_Mexikos.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="688" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dell%27Acqua_Ernennung_Maximilians_zum_Kaiser_Mexikos.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Maximilian_of_Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Maximilian of Habsburg">Maximilian</a> receiving a Mexican delegation at <a href="/wiki/Miramare" class="mw-redirect" title="Miramare">Miramar Castle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Trieste" title="Trieste">Trieste</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a></div></div></div>
<p>Between 1821 and 1910, Mexico battled through various civil wars between the established Conservative government and the Liberal reformists ("Mexico Timeline- Page 2)". On May 8, 1827 Baron Damas, the French Minister of Foreign Affairs, and Sebastián Camacho, a Mexican diplomat, signed an agreement called "The Declarations" which contained provisions regarding commerce and navigation between France and Mexico. At this time the French government did not recognize Mexico as an independent entity.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> It was not until 1861 that the liberalist rebels, led by Benito Juárez, took control of Mexico City, consolidating liberal rule. However, the constant state of warfare left Mexico with a tremendous amount of debt owed to Spain, England, and France, all of whom funded the Mexican war effort (Neeno). As newly appointed president, Benito Juárez suspended payment of debts for next two years, to focus on a rebuilding and stabilization initiative in Mexico under the new government. On December 8, 1861, Spain, England and France landed in Veracruz in order to seize unpaid debts from Mexico. However, Napoleon III, with intentions of establishing a French client state to further push his economic interests, pressured the other two powers to withdraw in 1862 (Greenspan; "French Intervention in Mexico…").
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Batalla_de_Puebla.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Batalla_de_Puebla.png/200px-Batalla_de_Puebla.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="262" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Batalla_de_Puebla.png/300px-Batalla_de_Puebla.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Batalla_de_Puebla.png/400px-Batalla_de_Puebla.png 2x" data-file-width="489" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Batalla_de_Puebla.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Painting depicting the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Puebla" title="Battle of Puebla">Battle of Puebla</a> in 1862</div></div></div>
<p>France under Napoleon III remained and established Maximilian of Habsburg, Archduke of Austria, as Emperor of Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The march by the French to Mexico City enticed heavy resistance by the Mexican government, it resulted in open warfare. The Battle of Puebla in 1862 in particular presented an important turning point in which Ignacio Zaragoza led the Mexican army to victory as they pushed back the French offensive ("Timeline of the Mexican Revolution"). The victory came to symbolize Mexico's power and national resolve against foreign occupancy and as a result delayed France's later attack on Mexico City for an entire year (Cinco de Mayo (Mexican History)). With heavy resistance by Mexican rebels and the fear of United States intervention against France, forced Napoleon III to withdraw from Mexico, leaving Maximilian to surrender, where he would be later executed by Mexican troops under the rule of Porfirio Díaz.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Napoleon III's desire to expand France's economic empire influenced the decision to seize territorial domain over the Central American region. The port city of Veracruz, Mexico and France's desire to construct a new canal were of particular interest. Bridging both New World and East Asian trade routes to the Atlantic were key to Napoleon III's economic goals to the mining of precious rocks and the expansion of France's textile industry. Napoleon's fear of the United States' economic influence over the Pacific trade region, and in turn all New World economic activity, pushed France to intervene in Mexico under the pretense of collecting on Mexico's debt. Eventually France began plans to build the Panama Canal in 1881 until 1904 when the United States took over and proceeded with its construction and implementation ("Read Our Story").
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_involvement_in_Latin_America_during_the_19th_century">American involvement in Latin America during the 19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: American involvement in Latin America during the 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Monroe_Doctrine">Monroe Doctrine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Monroe Doctrine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Doctrine" title="Monroe Doctrine">Monroe Doctrine</a> was included in President <a href="/wiki/James_Monroe" title="James Monroe">James Monroe</a>'s 1823 annual message to Congress. The doctrine warns European nations that the United States will no longer tolerate any new colonization of Latin American countries. It was originally drafted to meet the present major concerns, but eventually became the precept of U.S. foreign policy in the Western Hemisphere. The doctrine was put into effect in 1865 when the U.S. government supported Mexican president, <a href="/wiki/Benito_Ju%C3%A1rez" title="Benito Juárez">Benito Juárez</a>, diplomatically and militarily. Some Latin American countries viewed the U.S. interventions, allowed by the Monroe Doctrine when the U.S. deems necessary, with suspicion.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another important aspect of United States involvement in Latin America is the case of the <a href="/wiki/Filibuster_(military)" title="Filibuster (military)">filibuster</a> <a href="/wiki/William_Walker_(filibuster)" title="William Walker (filibuster)">William Walker</a>. In 1855, he traveled to Nicaragua hoping to overthrow the government and take the land for the United States. With only the aid of 56 followers, he was able to take over the city of <a href="/wiki/Granada,_Nicaragua" title="Granada, Nicaragua">Granada</a>, declaring himself commander of the army and installing <a href="/wiki/Patricio_Rivas" title="Patricio Rivas">Patricio Rivas</a> as a puppet president. However, Rivas's presidency ended when he fled Nicaragua; Walker rigged the following election to ensure that he became the next president. His presidency did not last long, however, as he was met with much opposition from political groups in Nicaragua and neighbouring countries. On May 1, 1857, Walker was forced by a coalition of Central American armies to surrender himself to a United States Navy officer who repatriated him and his followers. When Walker subsequently returned to Central America in 1860, he was apprehended by the Honduran authorities and executed.
</p>
<h4><span id="Mexican.E2.80.93American_War_.281846.E2.80.9348.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexican–American_War_(1846–48)">Mexican–American War (1846–48)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mexican–American War (1846–48)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexico_nebel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Mexico_nebel.jpg/250px-Mexico_nebel.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Mexico_nebel.jpg/375px-Mexico_nebel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Mexico_nebel.jpg/500px-Mexico_nebel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="999" data-file-height="652" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexico_nebel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>American occupation of <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a>, another instance of U.S. involvement in Latin America, was a war between the United States and Mexico that started in April 1846 and lasted until February 1848. The main cause of the war was the United States' annexation of Texas in 1845 and a dispute afterwards about whether the border between Mexico and the United States ended where Mexico claimed, at the <a href="/wiki/Nueces_River" title="Nueces River">Nueces River</a>, or ended where the United States claimed, at the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a>. Peace was negotiated between the United States and Mexico with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe_Hidalgo" title="Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo">Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo</a>, which stated that Mexico was to cede land which would later become part of California and New Mexico as well as give up all claims to Texas, for which the United States would pay $15,000,000. However, tensions between the two countries were still high and over the next six years things only got worse with raids along the border and attacks by Native Americans against Mexican citizens. To defuse the situation, the United States agreed to purchase 29,670 squares miles of land from Mexico for $10,000,000 so a southern railroad could be built to connect the Pacific and Atlantic coasts. This would become known as the <a href="/wiki/Gadsden_Purchase" title="Gadsden Purchase">Gadsden Purchase</a>. A critical component of U.S. intervention in Latin American affairs took form in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a>, which drastically affected the futures of Cuba and Puerto Rico in the Americas, as well as Guam and the Philippines, by dismantling some of the last remaining Spanish colonial possessions throughout the world.
</p>
<h2><span id="From_the_United_States_of_America_interventions_to_the_.22Good_Neighbor.22_policy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="From_the_United_States_of_America_interventions_to_the_&quot;Good_Neighbor&quot;_policy">From the United States of America interventions to the "Good Neighbor" policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: From the United States of America interventions to the &quot;Good Neighbor&quot; policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the late 19th century and early 20th century, the U.S. banana importing companies <a href="/wiki/United_Fruit_Company" title="United Fruit Company">United Fruit Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuyamel_Fruit_Company" title="Cuyamel Fruit Company">Cuyamel Fruit Company</a> (both ancestors of <a href="/wiki/Chiquita_Brands_International" title="Chiquita Brands International">Chiquita</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Standard_Fruit_Company" title="Standard Fruit Company">Standard Fruit Company</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Dole_Food_Company" title="Dole Food Company">Dole</a>), acquired large amounts of land in Central American countries like Guatemala, Honduras, and Costa Rica. The companies gained leverage over the governments and a ruling elite in these countries by dominating their economies and paying kickbacks, and exploited local workers. These countries came to be called <a href="/wiki/Banana_republic" title="Banana republic">banana republics</a>.
</p><p>The 1898 <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> resulted in the end of Spanish control in the Caribbean. A period of frequent U.S. intervention in Latin America followed, with the acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal_Zone" title="Panama Canal Zone">Panama Canal Zone</a> in 1903, the so-called <a href="/wiki/Banana_Wars" title="Banana Wars">Banana Wars</a> in Cuba, Haiti, Dominican Republic, Nicaragua, and Honduras; the <a href="/wiki/Caco_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Caco Wars">Caco Wars</a> in Haiti; and the so-called <a href="/wiki/Border_War_(1910%E2%80%931919)" class="mw-redirect" title="Border War (1910–1919)">Border War</a> with Mexico.
</p><p>After World War I, U.S. interventionism diminished, culminating in President <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Good_Neighbor_policy" title="Good Neighbor policy">Good Neighbor policy</a> in 1933.
</p>
<h3><span id="World_wars_.281914.E2.80.931945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World_wars_(1914–1945)">World wars (1914–1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: World wars (1914–1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="U.S._involvement_in_the_Mexican_Revolution" style="margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:25.5em;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;;padding:3px"><table class="nowraplinks navbox-vertical mw-collapsible mw-collapsed navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit"><tbody><tr><th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2" style="background-color:#C3D6EF;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Campaignbox_Battles_of_the_Mexican_Revolution_involving_the_United_States" title="Template:Campaignbox Battles of the Mexican Revolution involving the United States"><abbr title="View this template" style=";background-color:#C3D6EF;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; <ul><li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Columbus_(1916)" title="Battle of Columbus (1916)">Columbus</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_San_Isidro_(1916)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Battle of San Isidro (1916) (page does not exist)">San Isidro</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Aguacaliente&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Battle of Aguacaliente (page does not exist)">Aguacaliente</a></li>
