<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_culture" title="Latin American culture">Latin American culture</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Holy_Week_procession_Comayagua_Honduras_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Holy_Week_procession_Comayagua_Honduras_%281%29.jpg/220px-Holy_Week_procession_Comayagua_Honduras_%281%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Holy_Week_procession_Comayagua_Honduras_%281%29.jpg/330px-Holy_Week_procession_Comayagua_Honduras_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Holy_Week_procession_Comayagua_Honduras_%281%29.jpg/440px-Holy_Week_procession_Comayagua_Honduras_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="566" data-file-height="423" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Holy_Week_procession_Comayagua_Honduras_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Easter</a> procession in <a href="/wiki/Comayagua" title="Comayagua">Comayagua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg/170px-Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="308" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg/255px-Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg/340px-Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="1087" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaraguan</a> women wearing the <a href="/wiki/Mestizaje" class="mw-redirect" title="Mestizaje">Mestizaje</a> costume, which is a traditional costume worn to dance the Mestizaje dance. The costume demonstrates the Spanish influence upon <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaraguan</a> clothing.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Latin American culture is a mixture of many cultural expressions worldwide. It is the product of many diverse influences:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Indigenous</a> cultures of the people who inhabited the continent prior to European Colonization. Ancient and very advanced civilizations developed their own political, social and religious systems. The <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Mayas</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Aztec" class="mw-redirect" title="Aztec">Aztecs</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Inca_civilization" class="mw-redirect" title="Inca civilization">Incas</a> are examples of these. Indigenous legacies in music, dance, foods, arts and crafts, clothing, folk culture and traditions are very strong in Latin America. Linguistic effects on <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> are also marked, such as in terms like <a href="/wiki/Pampa" class="mw-redirect" title="Pampa">pampa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taco" title="Taco">taco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamale" title="Tamale">tamale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">cacique</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western civilization</a>, in particular the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Europe" title="Culture of Europe">culture of Europe</a>, was brought mainly by the colonial powers&#160;&#8211;&#32;the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32;between the 16th and 19th centuries. The most enduring European colonial influence is language and <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholicism</a>. More recently, additional cultural influences came from the United States and Europe during the nineteenth and twentieth centuries, due to the growing influence of the former on the world stage and immigration from the latter. The influence of the United States is particularly strong in northern Latin America, especially Puerto Rico, which is an American territory. Prior to 1959, Cuba, who fought for its independence along American soldiers in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a>, was also known to have a close socioeconomic relation with the United States. In addition, the United States also helped Panama become an independent state from Colombia and built the twenty-mile-long <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal_Zone" title="Panama Canal Zone">Panama Canal Zone</a> in Panama which held from 1903 (the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canal</a> opened to transoceanic freight traffic in 1914) to 1999, when the <a href="/wiki/Torrijos-Carter_Treaties" class="mw-redirect" title="Torrijos-Carter Treaties">Torrijos-Carter Treaties</a> restored Panamanian control of the Canal Zone. South America experienced waves of immigration of Europeans, especially Italians, Spaniards, Portuguese, Germans, Austrians, Poles, Ukrainians, French, Dutch, Russians, Croatians, Lithuanians and Ashkenazi Jews. With the end of colonialism, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_France" title="Culture of France">French culture</a> was also able to exert a direct influence in Latin America, especially in the realms of <a href="/wiki/High_culture" title="High culture">high culture</a>, science and medicine.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> This can be seen in any expression of the region's artistic traditions, including painting, literature and music, and in the realms of science and politics.</li></ul>
<p>Due to the impact of Enlightenment ideals after the French revolution, a certain number of Iberian-American countries decriminalized homosexuality after France and French territories in the Americas in 1791. Some of the countries that abolished sodomy laws or banned any reference to state interference in consensual adult sexuality in the 19th century were Dominican Republic (1822), Brazil (1824), Peru (1836), Mexico (1871), Paraguay (1880), Argentina (1887), Honduras (1899), Guatemala and El Salvador. Today same-sex marriage is legal in Argentina, Brazil, Colombia, Costa Rica, Ecuador, Uruguay, and French overseas departments, as well as in several states of Mexico. Civil unions can be held in Chile.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Africa" title="Culture of Africa">African cultures</a>, whose presence derives from a long history of <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">New World slavery</a>. Peoples of African descent have influenced the ethno-scapes of Latin America and the Caribbean. This is manifested for instance in music, dance and religion, especially in countries like Brazil, Uruguay, Honduras, Puerto Rico, Venezuela, Colombia, Panama, Haiti, Costa Rica, Dominican Republic, and Cuba.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Asia" title="Culture of Asia">Asian cultures</a>, whose part of the presence derives from the long history of the <a href="/wiki/Coolie" title="Coolie">Coolie trade</a> mostly arriving during the 19th and 20th centuries, and most commonly Chinese workers in Peru and Venezuela. But also from Japanese and Korean immigration especially headed to Brazil. This has largely effected the cuisine, traditions including literature, art and lifestyles and politics. The effects of Asian influences have especially and mostly effected the nations of The Dominican Republic, Brazil, Cuba, Panama and Peru.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_art" title="Latin American art">Latin American art</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Latin_American_artists" title="List of Latin American artists">List of Latin American artists</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RiveraMuralNationalPalace.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/RiveraMuralNationalPalace.jpg/220px-RiveraMuralNationalPalace.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/RiveraMuralNationalPalace.jpg/330px-RiveraMuralNationalPalace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/RiveraMuralNationalPalace.jpg/440px-RiveraMuralNationalPalace.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RiveraMuralNationalPalace.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Diego_Rivera" title="Diego Rivera">Diego Rivera</a>'s mural depicting Mexico's history at the <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_(Mexico)" title="National Palace (Mexico)">National Palace in Mexico City</a></div></div></div>
<p>Beyond the rich tradition of indigenous art, the development of Latin American visual art owed much to the influence of Spanish, Portuguese and French Baroque painting, which in turn often followed the trends of the Italian Masters. In general, this artistic Eurocentrism began to fade in the early twentieth century, as Latin Americans began to acknowledge the uniqueness of their condition and started to follow their own path.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Santiago_Martinez_Delgado_in_the_colombian_congress.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Santiago_Martinez_Delgado_in_the_colombian_congress.jpg/220px-Santiago_Martinez_Delgado_in_the_colombian_congress.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/28/Santiago_Martinez_Delgado_in_the_colombian_congress.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="330" data-file-height="275" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Santiago_Martinez_Delgado_in_the_colombian_congress.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mural by <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Martinez_Delgado" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiago Martinez Delgado">Santiago Martinez Delgado</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Congress" class="mw-redirect" title="Colombian Congress">Colombian Congress</a></div></div></div>
<p>From the early twentieth century, the art of Latin America was greatly inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Constructivism_(art)" title="Constructivism (art)">Constructivist Movement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The Movement quickly spread from Russia to Europe and then into Latin America. <a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Torres_Garc%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="Joaquín Torres García">Joaquín Torres García</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Rend%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Manuel Rendón">Manuel Rendón</a> have been credited with bringing the Constructivist Movement into Latin America from Europe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>An important artistic movement generated in Latin America is <i><a href="/wiki/Muralism" class="mw-redirect" title="Muralism">muralism</a></i> represented by <a href="/wiki/Diego_Rivera" title="Diego Rivera">Diego Rivera</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Alfaro_Siqueiros" title="David Alfaro Siqueiros">David Alfaro Siqueiros</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Clemente_Orozco" title="José Clemente Orozco">José Clemente Orozco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rufino_Tamayo" title="Rufino Tamayo">Rufino Tamayo</a> in Mexico, <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Martinez_Delgado" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiago Martinez Delgado">Santiago Martinez Delgado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Nel_G%C3%B3mez" title="Pedro Nel Gómez">Pedro Nel Gómez</a> in Colombia and <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Berni" title="Antonio Berni">Antonio Berni</a> in Argentina. Some of the most impressive <i>Muralista</i> works can be found in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, New York City, San Francisco, Los Angeles and <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>.
</p><p>Painter <a href="/wiki/Frida_Kahlo" title="Frida Kahlo">Frida Kahlo</a>, one of the most famous Mexican artists, painted about her own life and the Mexican culture in a style combining <a href="/wiki/Realism_(arts)" title="Realism (arts)">Realism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Symbolism_(arts)" title="Symbolism (arts)">Symbolism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surrealism" title="Surrealism">Surrealism</a>. Kahlo's work commands the highest selling price of all Latin American paintings.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Venezuelan <a href="/wiki/Armando_Rever%C3%B3n" title="Armando Reverón">Armando Reverón</a>, whose work begins to be recognized internationally, is one of the most important artists of the 20th century in South America; he is a precursor of <a href="/wiki/Arte_Povera" title="Arte Povera">Arte Povera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Happening" title="Happening">Happening</a>. From the 60s the kinetic art emerges in Venezuela, its main representatives are <a href="/wiki/Jes%C3%BAs_Soto" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesús Soto">Jesús Soto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Cruz-Diez" title="Carlos Cruz-Diez">Carlos Cruz-Diez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Otero" title="Alejandro Otero">Alejandro Otero</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gego" title="Gego">Gego</a>.
</p><p>Colombian <a href="/wiki/Sculptor" class="mw-redirect" title="Sculptor">sculptor</a> and painter <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Botero" title="Fernando Botero">Fernando Botero</a> is also widely known<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (May 2013)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> by his works which, on first examination, are noted for their exaggerated proportions and the corpulence of the human and animal figures.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_cinema" title="Latin American cinema">Latin American cinema</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guadalajara_international_Film_Festival.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Guadalajara_international_Film_Festival.jpg/220px-Guadalajara_international_Film_Festival.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Guadalajara_international_Film_Festival.jpg/330px-Guadalajara_international_Film_Festival.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Guadalajara_international_Film_Festival.jpg/440px-Guadalajara_international_Film_Festival.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guadalajara_international_Film_Festival.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Guadalajara_International_Film_Festival" title="Guadalajara International Film Festival">Guadalajara International Film Festival</a> is considered the most prestigious film festival in Latin America.</div></div></div>
<p>Latin American film is both rich and diverse. Historically, the main centers of production have been Mexico, Argentina, Brazil, and Cuba.  Latin American film flourished after sound was introduced in cinema, which added a linguistic barrier to the export of Hollywood film south of the border.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alejandro_Inarritu_Cannes_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Alejandro_Inarritu_Cannes_2017.jpg/170px-Alejandro_Inarritu_Cannes_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Alejandro_Inarritu_Cannes_2017.jpg/255px-Alejandro_Inarritu_Cannes_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Alejandro_Inarritu_Cannes_2017.jpg/340px-Alejandro_Inarritu_Cannes_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="674" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alejandro_Inarritu_Cannes_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Gonz%C3%A1lez_I%C3%B1%C3%A1rritu" title="Alejandro González Iñárritu">Alejandro González Iñárritu</a> became the second Mexican director in a row to win both the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Academy Award for Best Director">Academy Award</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Directors_Guild_of_America_Award" title="Directors Guild of America Award">Directors Guild of America Award</a> for Best Director. He won his second <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Oscar</a> in 2016 for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Revenant_(2015_film)" title="The Revenant (2015 film)">The Revenant</a></i>.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Mexico" title="Cinema of Mexico">Mexican cinema</a> started out in the silent era from 1896 to 1929 and flourished in the <a href="/wiki/Golden_age_of_the_cinema_of_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden age of the cinema of Mexico">Golden Era</a> of the 1940s. It boasted a huge industry comparable to <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">Hollywood</a> at the time with stars such as <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_F%C3%A9lix" title="María Félix">María Félix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo" title="Dolores del Río">Dolores del Río</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Infante" title="Pedro Infante">Pedro Infante</a>. In the 1970s,  Mexico was the location for many cult horror and action movies. More recently, films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Amores_Perros" class="mw-redirect" title="Amores Perros">Amores Perros</a></i> (2000) and <i><a href="/wiki/Y_tu_mam%C3%A1_tambi%C3%A9n" class="mw-redirect" title="Y tu mamá también">Y tu mamá también</a></i> (2001) enjoyed box office and critical acclaim and propelled <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Cuar%C3%B3n" title="Alfonso Cuarón">Alfonso Cuarón</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Gonz%C3%A1lez_I%C3%B1%C3%A1rritu" title="Alejandro González Iñárritu">Alejandro González Iñárritu</a> to the front rank of Hollywood directors. Alejandro González Iñárritu directed in 2010 <i><a href="/wiki/Biutiful" title="Biutiful">Biutiful</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Birdman_(film)" title="Birdman (film)"><i>Birdman</i></a> (2014), Alfonso Cuarón directed <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (film)">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a></i> in 2004 and <i><a href="/wiki/Gravity_(2013_film)" title="Gravity (2013 film)">Gravity</a></i> (2013).  Close friend of both, <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_del_Toro" title="Guillermo del Toro">Guillermo del Toro</a>, a top rank Hollywood director in Hollywood and Spain, directed <i><a href="/wiki/Pan%27s_Labyrinth" title="Pan&#39;s Labyrinth">Pan's Labyrinth</a></i> (2006) and produced <i><a href="/wiki/The_Orphanage_(2007_film)" title="The Orphanage (2007 film)">El Orfanato</a></i> (2007). <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Carrera" title="Carlos Carrera">Carlos Carrera</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Crime_of_Father_Amaro_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Crime of Father Amaro (film)">The Crime of Father Amaro</a>)</i>, and screenwriter <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Arriaga" title="Guillermo Arriaga">Guillermo Arriaga</a> are also some of the most known present-day Mexican film makers. <i><a href="/wiki/Rudo_y_Cursi" title="Rudo y Cursi">Rudo y Cursi</a></i> released in December (2008) in Mexico was directed by <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Cuar%C3%B3n" title="Carlos Cuarón">Carlos Cuarón</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cristina,_elenco_y_Oscar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Cristina%2C_elenco_y_Oscar.jpg/220px-Cristina%2C_elenco_y_Oscar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Cristina%2C_elenco_y_Oscar.jpg/330px-Cristina%2C_elenco_y_Oscar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Cristina%2C_elenco_y_Oscar.jpg/440px-Cristina%2C_elenco_y_Oscar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="386" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cristina,_elenco_y_Oscar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez" class="mw-redirect" title="Cristina Fernández">Cristina Fernández</a> with the film director <a href="/wiki/Juan_Jos%C3%A9_Campanella" title="Juan José Campanella">Juan José Campanella</a> and the cast of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Secret_in_Their_Eyes" title="The Secret in Their Eyes">The Secret in Their Eyes</a></i> (2009) with the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Foreign_Language_Film" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film">Oscar for Best Foreign Language Film</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Argentina" title="Cinema of Argentina">Argentine cinema</a> has also been prominenent since the first half of the 20th century and today averages over 60 full-length titles yearly. The industry suffered during the <a href="/wiki/Proceso_de_Reorganizaci%C3%B3n_Nacional" class="mw-redirect" title="Proceso de Reorganización Nacional">1976–1983 military dictatorship</a>; but re-emerged to produce the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Award</a> winner <i><a href="/wiki/The_Official_Story" title="The Official Story">The Official Story</a></i> in 1985. A wave of imported U.S. films again damaged the industry in the early 1990s, though it soon recovered, thriving even during the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_economic_crisis_(1999-2002)" class="mw-redirect" title="Argentine economic crisis (1999-2002)">Argentine economic crisis</a> around 2001. Many Argentine movies produced during recent years have been internationally acclaimed, including <i><a href="/wiki/Nueve_reinas" class="mw-redirect" title="Nueve reinas">Nueve reinas</a></i> (2000), <i><a href="/wiki/Son_of_the_Bride" title="Son of the Bride">Son of the Bride</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/El_abrazo_partido" class="mw-redirect" title="El abrazo partido">El abrazo partido</a></i> (2004), <i><a href="/wiki/El_otro" title="El otro">El otro</a></i> (2007), the 2010 Foreign Language <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Award</a> winner <i><a href="/wiki/El_secreto_de_sus_ojos" class="mw-redirect" title="El secreto de sus ojos">El secreto de sus ojos</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Wild_Tales_(film)" title="Wild Tales (film)">Wild Tales</a></i> (2014).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Brazil" title="Cinema of Brazil">In Brazil</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Cinema_Novo" title="Cinema Novo">Cinema Novo</a></i> movement created a particular way of making movies with critical and intellectual screenplays, a clearer photography related to the light of the outdoors in a tropical landscape, and a political message. The modern Brazilian film industry has become more profitable inside the country, and some of its productions have received prizes and recognition in Europe and the United States, with movies such as <i><a href="/wiki/Central_do_Brasil_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Central do Brasil (film)">Central do Brasil</a></i> (1999), <i><a href="/wiki/City_of_God_(2002_film)" title="City of God (2002 film)">Cidade de Deus</a></i> (2002) and <i><a href="/wiki/Tropa_de_Elite" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropa de Elite">Tropa de Elite</a></i> (2007).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Cinema of Puerto Rico">Puerto Rican cinema</a> has produced some notable films, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Una_Aventura_Llamada_Menudo" class="mw-redirect" title="Una Aventura Llamada Menudo">Una Aventura Llamada Menudo</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Diaz_de_Doris" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Diaz de Doris">Los Diaz de Doris</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Casi_Casi" title="Casi Casi">Casi Casi</a></i>. An influx of Hollywood films affected the local film industry in Puerto Rico during the 1980s and 1990s, but several Puerto Rican films have been produced since and it has been recovering.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Cuba" title="Cinema of Cuba">Cuban cinema</a> has enjoyed much official support since the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuban revolution">Cuban revolution</a> and important film-makers include <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Guti%C3%A9rrez_Alea" title="Tomás Gutiérrez Alea">Tomás Gutiérrez Alea</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_literature" title="Latin American literature">Latin American literature</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Latin_American_writers" title="List of Latin American writers">List of Latin American writers</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_(1772).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_%281772%29.jpg/170px-Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_%281772%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_%281772%29.jpg/255px-Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_%281772%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_%281772%29.jpg/340px-Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_%281772%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="968" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_(1772).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz" class="mw-redirect" title="Sor Juana Inés de la Cruz">Sor Juana Inés de la Cruz</a> in 1772 by Andrés de Islas</div></div></div>
<p>Pre-Columbian cultures were primarily oral, though the Aztecs and Mayans, for instance, produced elaborate <a href="/wiki/Aztec_codices" title="Aztec codices">codices</a>. Oral accounts of mythological and religious beliefs were also sometimes recorded after the arrival of European colonizers, as was the case with the <a href="/wiki/Popol_Vuh" title="Popol Vuh">Popol Vuh</a>. Moreover, a tradition of oral narrative survives to this day, for instance among the <a href="/wiki/Quechua_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Quechua languages">Quechua</a>-speaking population of Peru and the <a href="/wiki/K%27iche%27_people" class="mw-redirect" title="K&#39;iche&#39; people">Quiché (K'iche')</a> of Guatemala.
</p><p>From the very moment of Europe's discovery of the continents, early explorers and <a href="/wiki/Conquistadores" class="mw-redirect" title="Conquistadores">conquistadores</a> produced written accounts and crónicas of their experience&#160;&#8211;&#32;such as <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Columbus</a>'s letters or <a href="/wiki/Bernal_D%C3%ADaz_del_Castillo" title="Bernal Díaz del Castillo">Bernal Díaz del Castillo</a>'s description of the conquest of Mexico. During the colonial period, written culture was often in the hands of the church, within which context <a href="/wiki/Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz" class="mw-redirect" title="Sor Juana Inés de la Cruz">Sor Juana Inés de la Cruz</a> wrote memorable poetry and philosophical essays. Towards the end of the 18th Century and the beginning of the 19th, a distinctive <a href="/wiki/Criollo_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Criollo (people)">criollo</a> literary tradition emerged, including the first novels such as Lizardi's <i><a href="/wiki/El_Periquillo_Sarniento" class="mw-redirect" title="El Periquillo Sarniento">El Periquillo Sarniento</a></i> (1816).
</p><p>The 19th century was a period of "foundational fictions" (in critic Doris Sommer's words), novels in the <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">Romantic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Naturalism_(literature)" title="Naturalism (literature)">Naturalist</a> traditions that attempted to establish a sense of national identity, and which often focussed on the indigenous question or the dichotomy of "civilization or barbarism" (for which see, say, <a href="/wiki/Domingo_Faustino_Sarmiento" title="Domingo Faustino Sarmiento">Domingo Sarmiento</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Facundo" title="Facundo">Facundo</a></i> (1845), <a href="/wiki/Juan_Le%C3%B3n_Mera" title="Juan León Mera">Juan León Mera</a>'s <i>Cumandá</i> (1879), or <a href="/wiki/Euclides_da_Cunha" title="Euclides da Cunha">Euclides da Cunha</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Os_Sert%C3%B5es" title="Os Sertões">Os Sertões</a></i> (1902)). The 19th century also witnessed the realist work of <a href="/wiki/Machado_de_Assis" title="Machado de Assis">Machado de Assis</a>, who made use of surreal devices of metaphor and playful narrative construction, much admired by critic <a href="/wiki/Harold_Bloom" title="Harold Bloom">Harold Bloom</a>.
</p><p>At the turn of the 20th century, <i><a href="/wiki/Modernismo" title="Modernismo">modernismo</a></i> emerged, a poetic movement whose founding text was Nicaraguan poet <a href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A9n_Dar%C3%ADo" title="Rubén Darío">Rubén Darío</a>'s <i>Azul</i> (1888). This was the first Latin American literary movement to influence literary culture outside of the region, and was also the first truly Latin American literature, in that national differences were no longer so much at issue. <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mart%C3%AD" title="José Martí">José Martí</a>, for instance, though a Cuban patriot, also lived in Mexico and the United States and wrote for journals in Argentina and elsewhere.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gabriela_Mistral-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Gabriela_Mistral-01.jpg/170px-Gabriela_Mistral-01.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Gabriela_Mistral-01.jpg/255px-Gabriela_Mistral-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Gabriela_Mistral-01.jpg/340px-Gabriela_Mistral-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1705" data-file-height="2300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gabriela_Mistral-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chilean poet <a href="/wiki/Gabriela_Mistral" title="Gabriela Mistral">Gabriela Mistral</a>, first Latin American to win a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a>, in 1945</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jorge_Luis_Borges_Hotel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Jorge_Luis_Borges_Hotel.jpg/170px-Jorge_Luis_Borges_Hotel.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Jorge_Luis_Borges_Hotel.jpg/255px-Jorge_Luis_Borges_Hotel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Jorge_Luis_Borges_Hotel.jpg/340px-Jorge_Luis_Borges_Hotel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="526" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jorge_Luis_Borges_Hotel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Argentine <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Luis_Borges" title="Jorge Luis Borges">Jorge Luis Borges</a> in <a href="/wiki/L%27H%C3%B4tel" title="L&#39;Hôtel">L'Hôtel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> in 1969</div></div></div>
<p>However, what really put Latin American literature on the global map was no doubt the literary <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Boom" title="Latin American Boom">boom</a> of the 1960s and 1970s, distinguished by daring and experimental novels (such as <a href="/wiki/Julio_Cort%C3%A1zar" title="Julio Cortázar">Julio Cortázar</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Hopscotch_(Julio_Cort%C3%A1zar_novel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hopscotch (Julio Cortázar novel)">Rayuela</a></i> (1963)) that were frequently published in Spain and quickly translated into English. The Boom's defining novel was <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Garc%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1rquez" title="Gabriel García Márquez">Gabriel García Márquez</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/One_Hundred_Years_of_Solitude" title="One Hundred Years of Solitude">Cien años de soledad</a></i> (1967), which led to the association of Latin American literature with <a href="/wiki/Magic_realism" title="Magic realism">magic realism</a>, though other important writers of the period such as the Peruvian <a href="/wiki/Mario_Vargas_Llosa" title="Mario Vargas Llosa">Mario Vargas Llosa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Fuentes" title="Carlos Fuentes">Carlos Fuentes</a> do not fit so easily within this framework. Arguably, the Boom's culmination was <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Roa_Bastos" title="Augusto Roa Bastos">Augusto Roa Bastos</a>'s monumental <i>Yo, el supremo</i> (1974). In the wake of the Boom, influential precursors such as <a href="/wiki/Juan_Rulfo" title="Juan Rulfo">Juan Rulfo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alejo_Carpentier" title="Alejo Carpentier">Alejo Carpentier</a>, and above all <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Luis_Borges" title="Jorge Luis Borges">Jorge Luis Borges</a> were also rediscovered.
</p><p>Contemporary literature in the region is vibrant and varied, ranging from the best-selling <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Coelho" title="Paulo Coelho">Paulo Coelho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isabel_Allende" title="Isabel Allende">Isabel Allende</a> to the more avant-garde and critically acclaimed work of writers such as <a href="/wiki/Diamela_Eltit" title="Diamela Eltit">Diamela Eltit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giannina_Braschi" title="Giannina Braschi">Giannina Braschi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Piglia" title="Ricardo Piglia">Ricardo Piglia</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Bola%C3%B1o" title="Roberto Bolaño">Roberto Bolaño</a>. There has also been considerable attention paid to the genre of <a href="/wiki/Testimony#Literature" title="Testimony">testimonio</a>, texts produced in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Subaltern_(postcolonialism)" title="Subaltern (postcolonialism)">subaltern</a> subjects such as <a href="/wiki/Rigoberta_Mench%C3%BA" title="Rigoberta Menchú">Rigoberta Menchú</a>. Finally, a new breed of chroniclers is represented by the more journalistic <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Monsiv%C3%A1is" title="Carlos Monsiváis">Carlos Monsiváis</a> and Pedro Lemebel.
</p><p>The region boasts six <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize winners</a>: in addition to the two Chilean poets <a href="/wiki/Gabriela_Mistral" title="Gabriela Mistral">Gabriela Mistral</a> (1945) and <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Neruda" title="Pablo Neruda">Pablo Neruda</a> (1971), there is also the Guatemalan novelist <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Angel_Asturias" class="mw-redirect" title="Miguel Angel Asturias">Miguel Angel Asturias</a> (1967), the Colombian writer <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Garc%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1rquez" title="Gabriel García Márquez">Gabriel García Márquez</a> (1982),  the Mexican poet and essayist <a href="/wiki/Octavio_Paz" title="Octavio Paz">Octavio Paz</a> (1990), and the Peruvian novelist <a href="/wiki/Mario_Vargas_Llosa" title="Mario Vargas Llosa">Mario Vargas Llosa</a> (2010).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Music and dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Latin_America" title="Music of Latin America">Music of Latin America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_pop" title="Latin pop">Latin pop</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Latin_dance" title="Latin dance">Latin dance</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Salsa_en_Cali.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Salsa_en_Cali.jpg/170px-Salsa_en_Cali.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Salsa_en_Cali.jpg/255px-Salsa_en_Cali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Salsa_en_Cali.jpg/340px-Salsa_en_Cali.jpg 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Salsa_en_Cali.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Salsa_(dance)" title="Salsa (dance)">Salsa</a> dancing in <a href="/wiki/Cali" title="Cali">Cali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a></div></div></div>
<p>Latin America has produced many successful worldwide artists in terms of recorded global music sales. Among the most successful have been <a href="/wiki/Juan_Gabriel" title="Juan Gabriel">Juan Gabriel</a> (Mexico) only Latin American musician to have sold over 200 million records worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Estefan" title="Gloria Estefan">Gloria Estefan</a> (Cuba), <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Santana" title="Carlos Santana">Carlos Santana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Miguel" title="Luis Miguel">Luis Miguel</a> (Mexico) of whom have sold over 90 million records, <a href="/wiki/Shakira" title="Shakira">Shakira</a> (Colombia) and <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Vicente Fernández">Vicente Fernández</a> (Mexico) with over 50 million records sold worldwide. <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Iglesias" title="Enrique Iglesias">Enrique Iglesias</a>, although not a Latin American, has also contributed for the success of Latin music.
</p><p>Other notable successful mainstream acts through the years, include <a href="/wiki/RBD" title="RBD">RBD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celia_Cruz" title="Celia Cruz">Celia Cruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soda_Stereo" title="Soda Stereo">Soda Stereo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thal%C3%ADa" title="Thalía">Thalía</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Martin" title="Ricky Martin">Ricky Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Man%C3%A1" title="Maná">Maná</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marc_Anthony" title="Marc Anthony">Marc Anthony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Arjona" title="Ricardo Arjona">Ricardo Arjona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Selena" title="Selena">Selena</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Menudo_(band)" title="Menudo (band)">Menudo</a>.
</p><p>Caribbean Hispanic music, such as <a href="/wiki/Merengue_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Merengue (music)">merengue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bachata_(music)" title="Bachata (music)">bachata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salsa_music" title="Salsa music">salsa</a>, and more recently <a href="/wiki/Reggaeton" title="Reggaeton">reggaeton</a>, from such countries as the Dominican Republic, Puerto Rico, Trinidad and Tobago, Cuba, and Panama, has been strongly influenced by African rhythms and melodies. Haiti's <a href="/wiki/Compas" title="Compas">compas</a> is a genre of music that is influenced by its Caribbean Hispanic counterparts, along with elements of jazz and modern sounds.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JarabeTapatio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/JarabeTapatio.jpg/170px-JarabeTapatio.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b2/JarabeTapatio.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="221" data-file-height="300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JarabeTapatio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traditional Mexican dance <a href="/wiki/Jarabe_Tapat%C3%ADo" title="Jarabe Tapatío">Jarabe Tapatío</a></div></div></div>
<p>Another well-known Latin American musical genre includes the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_tango" title="Argentine tango">Argentine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uruguayan_tango" title="Uruguayan tango">Uruguayan tango</a> (with <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Gardel" title="Carlos Gardel">Carlos Gardel</a> as the greatest exponent), as well as the distinct <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_tango" title="Nuevo tango">nuevo tango</a>, a fusion of tango, <a href="/wiki/Acoustic_music" title="Acoustic music">acoustic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic music</a> popularized by <a href="/wiki/Bandone%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Bandoneón">bandoneón</a> virtuoso <a href="/wiki/%C3%81stor_Piazzolla" class="mw-redirect" title="Ástor Piazzolla">Ástor Piazzolla</a>. <a href="/wiki/Samba" title="Samba">Samba</a>, North American <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_classical_music" class="mw-redirect" title="European classical music">European classical music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Choro" title="Choro">choro</a> combined to form <i><a href="/wiki/Bossa_nova" title="Bossa nova">bossa nova</a></i> in Brazil, popularized by <a href="/wiki/Guitar" title="Guitar">guitarist</a> <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Gilberto" title="João Gilberto">João Gilberto</a> with singer <a href="/wiki/Astrud_Gilberto" title="Astrud Gilberto">Astrud Gilberto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jazz_piano" title="Jazz piano">pianist</a> <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Carlos_Jobim" class="mw-redirect" title="Antonio Carlos Jobim">Antonio Carlos Jobim</a>.
</p><p>Other influential Latin American sounds include the Antillean <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">soca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">calypso</a>, the Honduran (Garifuna) <a href="/wiki/Punta" title="Punta">punta</a>, the Colombian <a href="/wiki/Cumbia" title="Cumbia">cumbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vallenato" title="Vallenato">vallenato</a>, the Chilean <a href="/wiki/Cueca" title="Cueca">cueca</a>, the Ecuadorian <a href="/w/index.php?title=Boleros_music&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Boleros music (page does not exist)">boleros</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockoleras&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rockoleras (page does not exist)">rockoleras</a>, the Mexican <a href="/wiki/Ranchera" title="Ranchera">ranchera</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mariachi" title="Mariachi">mariachi</a> which is the epitome of Mexican soul, the Nicaraguan <a href="/wiki/Palo_de_Mayo" title="Palo de Mayo">palo de Mayo</a>, the Peruvian <a href="/wiki/Marinera" title="Marinera">marinera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tondero" title="Tondero">tondero</a>, the Uruguayan <a href="/wiki/Candombe" title="Candombe">candombe</a>, the French Antillean <a href="/wiki/Zouk" title="Zouk">zouk</a> (derived from Haitian compas) and the various styles of music from pre-Columbian traditions that are widespread in the <a href="/wiki/Andean" class="mw-redirect" title="Andean">Andean</a> region.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG/170px-Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG/255px-Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG/340px-Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG 2x" data-file-width="957" data-file-height="1245" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carmen_Miranda_1941.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Brazilian singer <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Miranda" title="Carmen Miranda">Carmen Miranda</a> helped popularize <a href="/wiki/Samba" title="Samba">samba</a> internationally.</div></div></div>
<p>The classical composer <a href="/wiki/Heitor_Villa-Lobos" title="Heitor Villa-Lobos">Heitor Villa-Lobos</a> (1887–1959) worked on the recording of native musical traditions within his homeland of Brazil. The traditions of his homeland heavily influenced his classical works.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Also notable is the recent work of the Cuban <a href="/wiki/Leo_Brouwer" title="Leo Brouwer">Leo Brouwer</a> and guitar work of the Venezuelan <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Lauro" title="Antonio Lauro">Antonio Lauro</a> and the Paraguayan <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_Barrios" title="Agustín Barrios">Agustín Barrios</a>. Latin America has also produced world-class classical performers such as the Chilean pianist <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Arrau" title="Claudio Arrau">Claudio Arrau</a>, Brazilian pianist <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Freire" title="Nelson Freire">Nelson Freire</a> and the Argentine pianist and conductor <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Barenboim" title="Daniel Barenboim">Daniel Barenboim</a>. Brazilian opera soprano <a href="/wiki/Bidu_Say%C3%A3o" title="Bidu Sayão">Bidu Sayão</a>, one of Brazil's most famous musicians, was a leading artist of the Metropolitan Opera in New York City from 1937 to 1952.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg/170px-Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg/255px-Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg/340px-Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tango-Show-Buenos-Aires-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A couple dances <a href="/wiki/Tango_(dance)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tango (dance)">tango</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Arguably, the main contribution to music entered through folklore, where the true soul of the Latin American and Caribbean countries is expressed. Musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Yma_S%C3%BAmac" class="mw-redirect" title="Yma Súmac">Yma Súmac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chabuca_Granda" title="Chabuca Granda">Chabuca Granda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atahualpa_Yupanqui" title="Atahualpa Yupanqui">Atahualpa Yupanqui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Violeta_Parra" title="Violeta Parra">Violeta Parra</a>, <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Jara" title="Víctor Jara">Víctor Jara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Cafrune" title="Jorge Cafrune">Jorge Cafrune</a>, <a href="/wiki/Facundo_Cabral" title="Facundo Cabral">Facundo Cabral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes_Sosa" title="Mercedes Sosa">Mercedes Sosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Negrete" title="Jorge Negrete">Jorge Negrete</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luiz_Gonzaga" title="Luiz Gonzaga">Luiz Gonzaga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caetano_Veloso" title="Caetano Veloso">Caetano Veloso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Susana_Baca" title="Susana Baca">Susana Baca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chavela_Vargas" title="Chavela Vargas">Chavela Vargas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Diaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Simon Diaz">Simon Diaz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julio_Jaramillo" title="Julio Jaramillo">Julio Jaramillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toto_la_Momposina" class="mw-redirect" title="Toto la Momposina">Toto la Momposina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gilberto_Gil" title="Gilberto Gil">Gilberto Gil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Beth%C3%A2nia" title="Maria Bethânia">Maria Bethânia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nana_Caymmi" title="Nana Caymmi">Nana Caymmi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nara_Le%C3%A3o" title="Nara Leão">Nara Leão</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gal_Costa" title="Gal Costa">Gal Costa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ney_Matogrosso" title="Ney Matogrosso">Ney Matogrosso</a> as well as musical ensembles such as <a href="/wiki/Inti_Illimani" class="mw-redirect" title="Inti Illimani">Inti Illimani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Los_Kjarkas" title="Los Kjarkas">Los Kjarkas</a> are magnificent examples of the heights that this soul can reach.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Latin_pop" title="Latin pop">Latin pop</a>, including many forms of <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a>, is popular in Latin America today (see <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_rock_and_roll" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish language rock and roll">Spanish language rock and roll</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>  A few examples are <a href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_Tacuba" title="Café Tacuba">Café Tacuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soda_Stereo" title="Soda Stereo">Soda Stereo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Man%C3%A1" title="Maná">Maná</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rita_Lee" title="Rita Lee">Rita Lee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mutantes" class="mw-redirect" title="Mutantes">Mutantes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secos_e_Molhados" class="mw-redirect" title="Secos e Molhados">Secos e Molhados</a> <a href="/wiki/Legi%C3%A3o_Urbana" title="Legião Urbana">Legião Urbana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tit%C3%A3s" title="Titãs">Titãs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paralamas_do_Sucesso" class="mw-redirect" title="Paralamas do Sucesso">Paralamas do Sucesso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cazuza" title="Cazuza">Cazuza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bar%C3%A3o_Vermelho" title="Barão Vermelho">Barão Vermelho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skank_(band)" title="Skank (band)">Skank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miranda!" title="Miranda!">Miranda!</a>, <a href="/wiki/CSS_(band)" title="CSS (band)">Cansei de Ser Sexy or CSS</a>, and Bajo Fondo.
</p><p>More recently, reggaeton, which blends Jamaican reggae and dancehall with Latin America genres such as <a href="/wiki/Bomba_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Bomba (Puerto Rico)">bomba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plena" title="Plena">plena</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a>, is becoming more popular, in spite of the controversy surrounding its lyrics, dance steps (<a href="/wiki/Perreo" class="mw-redirect" title="Perreo">Perreo</a>) and music videos. It has become very popular among populations with a "migrant culture" influence&#160;– both Latino populations in the United States, such as southern Florida and New York City, and parts of Latin America where migration to the United States is common, such as Trinidad and Tobago, Dominican Republic, Colombia, Ecuador, El Salvador, and Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Heritage_sites">World Heritage sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: World Heritage sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-a-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-a_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-a_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">In the main Latin American languages:
<ul><li>Spanish: <i lang="es">América Latina</i> or <i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Latinoamérica</i></li>
<li>Portuguese: <i lang="pt">América Latina</i></li>
<li>French: <i lang="fr">Amérique Latine</i></li></ul>
</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-d-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-d_4-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-d_4-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Includes the population estimates for South American and Central American countries excluding Belize, Guyana, the United States, and Spanish and French speaking Caribbean countries and territories, as listed under "<a href="/wiki/Latin_America#Subregions_and_countries" title="Latin America">Sub-regions and countries</a>"</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-c-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-c_5-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Not including Anglophone or Dutch-speaking countries, such as <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>; see <a href="#Contemporary_definitions">Contemporary definitions</a> section</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-Gutierrez-2016-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Gutierrez-2016_23-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Gutierrez, Ramon A. (23 August 2016). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/GutierrezPp.1953Notes/Gutierrez%20pp.%2019-53%20notes_djvu.txt">"1. What's in a Name?"</a>.  In Gutierrez, Ramon A.; Almaguer, Tomas (eds.). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=8IahDAAAQBAJ"><i>The New Latino Studies Reader: A Twenty-First-Century Perspective</i></a> (1st ed.). Berkeley: University of California Press. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-520-96051-0" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-520-96051-0"><bdi>978-0-520-96051-0</bdi></a>. <a href="/wiki/OCLC" title="OCLC">OCLC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/oclc/1043876740">1043876740</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">6 August</span> 2019</span>. <q>The word latinoamericano emerged in the years following the wars of independence in Spain's former colonies. ... By the late 1850s, Californios were writing in newspapers about their membership in America latina (Latin America) and latinoamerica, calling themselves latinos as the shortened name for their hemispheric membership in la raza latina (the Latin race). Reprinting an 1858 opinion piece by a correspondent in Havana on race relations in the Americas, El Clamor Publico of Los Angeles surmised that 'two rival races are competing with each other ... the Anglo Saxon and the Latin one [la raza latina].'<span style="white-space:nowrap">&#8201;</span></q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=1.+What%27s+in+a+Name%3F&amp;rft.btitle=The+New+Latino+Studies+Reader%3A+A+Twenty-First-Century+Perspective&amp;rft.place=Berkeley&amp;rft.edition=1st&amp;rft.pub=University+of+California+Press&amp;rft.date=2016-08-23&amp;rft_id=info%3Aoclcnum%2F1043876740&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-520-96051-0&amp;rft.aulast=Gutierrez&amp;rft.aufirst=Ramon+A.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fstream%2FGutierrezPp.1953Notes%2FGutierrez%2520pp.%252019-53%2520notes_djvu.txt&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALatin+America" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-125"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-125">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/16086/16086-h/16086-h.htm">Letter from Fajardo to Felipe III From Manila, August 15 1620.(From the Spanish Archives of the Indies)</a>("The infantry does not amount to two hundred men, in three companies. If these men were that number, and Spaniards, it would not be so bad; but, although I have not seen them, because they have not yet arrived here, I am told that they are, as at other times, for the most part boys, mestizos, and mulattoes, with some Indians (Native Americans). There is no little cause for regret in the great sums that reënforcements of such men waste for, and cost, your Majesty. I cannot see what betterment there will be until your Majesty shall provide it, since I do not think, that more can be done in Nueva Spaña, although the viceroy must be endeavoring to do so, as he is ordered.")</span>

<li>Moreira, Igor A. G. <i>O Espaço Geográfico, geografia geral e do Brasil</i>. 18. Ed. São Paulo: Ática, 1981. <span class="languageicon">(in Portuguese)</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Leddy_Phelan" title="John Leddy Phelan">Phelan, John Leddy</a>. (1968). <i>Pan-latinisms, French Intervention in Mexico (1861–1867) and the Genesis of the Idea of Latin America</i>. Mexico City: Universidad Nacional Autonónoma de México 1968.</li>
<li>Vesentini, José William. <i>Brasil, sociedade e espaço – Geografia do Brasil</i>. 7th Ed. São Paulo: Ática, 1988. <span class="languageicon">(in Portuguese)</span></li>
<li>Tenenbaum, Barbara A. ed. <i>Encyclopedia of Latin American History and Culture.</i> 5 vols. New York:  Charles Scribner’s Sons 1996</li>
<li>Tenorio-Trillo, Mauricio. <i>Latin America: The Allure and Power of an Idea</i>. Chicago: University of Chicago Press 2017.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Vasconcelos" title="José Vasconcelos">Vasconcelos, José</a>. <i>Indología: Una interpretación de la cultura ibero-americana</i>. Barcelona: Agencia Mundial de Librería 1927.</li>
<li>Werncek vianna, Luiz. <i>A revolução passive: Iberismo e americanismo no Brasil</i>. Rio de Janeiro: Editora Revan 1997.</li>
<li>Zea, Leopoldo. <i>Filosofía de la historia americana</i>. Mexico City: Fondo de Cultura Económico 1978.</li>
